This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\\n226: // stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\\n227: func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\\n228: \\tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\\n229: \\tif err != nil {\\n230: \\t\\tpanic(err)\\n231: \\t}\\n232: \\tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\\n233: \\t\\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\\n234: \\t}\\n235: \\tle.Run(ctx)\\n236: }\\n237: \\n238: // GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\\n239: // no leader has yet been observed.\\n240: // This function is for informational purposes. endpoints object to store the record of the\\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n155: \t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n156: \t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n157: \t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n158: \tReleaseOnCancel bool\n159: \n160: \t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n161: \tName string\n162: \n163: \t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n164: \t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n165: \tCoordinated bool\n166: }\n167: \n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n170: //\n171: // possible future callbacks:\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n174: \t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n175: \tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n176: \t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n177: \t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n178: \t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n179: \t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n180: \tOnStoppedLeading func()\n181: \t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n182: \t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n183: \t// leader when the client starts.\n184: \tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n185: }\n186: \n187: // LeaderElector is a leader election client.\n188: type LeaderElector struct {\n189: \tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n190: \t// internal bookkeeping\n191: \tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n192: \tobservedRawRecord []byte\n193: \tobservedTime      time.Time\n194: \t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n195: \t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n196: \t// not yet been reported.\n197: \treportedLeader string\n198: \n199: \t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n200: \tclock clock.Clock\n201: \n202: \t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n203: \tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n204: \n205: \tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n206: }\n207: \n208: // Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n209: // before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n210: // stopped holding the leader lease\n211: func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n212: \tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n213: \tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n214: \n215: \tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n216: \t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n217: \t}\n218: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n219: \tdefer cancel()\n220: \tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n221: \tle.renew(ctx)\n222: }\n223: \n224: // RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n225: // fails to validate. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\n226: // stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\n227: func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\n228: \tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\n229: \tif err != nil {\n230: \t\tpanic(err)\n231: \t}\n232: \tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\n233: \t\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\n234: \t}\n235: \tle.Run(ctx)\n236: }\n237: \n238: // GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\n239: // no leader has yet been observed.\n240: // This function is for informational purposes. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\n241: func (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\n242: \treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\n243: }\n244: \n245: // IsLeader returns true if the last observed leader was this client else returns false.\n246: func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\n247: \treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\n248: }\n249: \n250: // acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n251: // Returns false if ctx signals done.\n252: func (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx context.Context) bool {\n253: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n254: \tdefer cancel()\n255: \tsucceeded := false\n256: \tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n257: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n258: \tlogger.Info(\"Attempting to acquire leader lease...\", \"lock\", desc)\n259: \twait.JitterUntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n260: \t\tif succeeded\n276: }\n277: \n278: // renew loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew fails or ctx signals done.\n279: func (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx err error) {\n286: \t\t\t// PollUntilContextTimeout invokes condition even when the context is canceled when immediate=true.\n287: \t\t\t// Short-circuit this to prevent unnecessary processing and error log messages.\n288: \t\t\tif err := ctx.Err(); err != nil {\n289: \t\t\t\treturn false, err\n290: \t\t\t}\n291: \t\t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n292: \t\t\t\treturn le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx), nil\n293: \t\t\t} else {\n294: \t\t\t\treturn le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx), nil\n295: \t\t\t}\n296: \t\t})\n297: \t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n298: \t\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n299: \t\tif err == nil {\n300: \t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Successfully renewed lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n301: Once a leader is established, it maintains the lease by renewing within the RenewDeadline window. If renewal fails before LeaseDuration expires, the lease becomes available for other candidates. Non-leaders monitor lease updates to detect when leadership changes hands.\n\n## etcd (Raft-based Leader Election)\n\nThe implementation spans several core components: `raftNode` in `server/etcdserver/raft.go` handles Raft consensus and leader state, while `EtcdServer` in `server/etcdserver/server.go` exposes leader-related methods. Leadership is enforced at the RPC layer through `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/interceptor.go`, and peer communication occurs via `server/etcdserver/api/rafthttp/transport.go` which tracks leader statistics. Configuration parameters like ElectionTicks and TickMs are defined in `server/config/config.go`, and clients interact with the election API through `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`.\n\nKey operations include `raftNode.start()` which initializes the Raft node and monitors leadership transitions, `raftNode.tick()` which drives the election timeout mechanism, and `EtcdServer.Lead()` to retrieve the current leader. Leadership can be manually transferred via `EtcdServer.MoveLeader()` or gracefully during shutdown through `EtcdServer.TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()`. The `updateLeadership()` callback fires when leadership changes, while `LeaderStats` maintains metrics on leader and follower activity. Clients use `Election.Campaign()` to participate in leadership elections.\n\nThe election process works by having followers timeout and initiate campaigns using Raft's voting mechanism, with the winning node becoming leader and broadcasting heartbeats to maintain authority. When a leader stops sending heartbeats, followers detect this through election timeout and begin campaigning. LeaderElector (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go)**\\n- Main client responsible for acquiring and renewing leadership leases\\n- Operates with three time-based parameters: LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod\\n- Maintains observedRecord tracking current lease holder identity\\n\\n**2. LeaderElectionRecord (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go)**\\n- Stores: HolderIdentity, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaseDurationSeconds, LeaderTransitions\\n- Transitions count increments each time leadership changes, useful for detecting failovers\\n\\n**3. Lease-Based Coordination (pkg/apis/coordination/types.go)**\\n- Uses Kubernetes Lease API (coordination.k8s.io/v1)\\n- Modern approach also supports Coordinated Leader Election with LeaseCandidate objects for picking best leader\\n- Supports multiple election strategies: OldestEmulationVersion strategy for version-aware selection\\n\\n### Leadership Acquisition and Renewal Flow\\n\\n**Acquisition Phase (leaderelection.go:acquire())**\\n- Loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew() with exponential backoff (RetryPeriod base, 1.2x jitter)\\n- First successful update creates the lease or updates it if expired\\n\\n**Renewal Phase (leaderelection.go:renew())**\\n- Leader continuously renews within RenewDeadline timeout\\n- Fast path: Optimistic update using last observed record\\n- Slow path: Fetch fresh record, verify ownership, then update\\n- Updates RenewTime to extend lease validity\\n\\n**Failover Detection (leaderelection.go:isLeaseValid())**\\n- Non-leaders observe lease and detect expiry\\n- Lease expires when: RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds < now\\n- Failed leader detected when renewals fail (e.g., leader unreachable, cannot reach API server)\\n- Default timings: LeaseDuration=15s, RenewDeadline=10s, RetryPeriod=2s\\n\\n### Health Monitoring\\n- HealthzAdaptor tracks if current leader is failing to renew within tolerance\\n- LeaderCallbacks notify: OnStartedLeading, OnStoppedLeading, OnNewLeader\\n- Metrics track leader_election_master_status and slowpath_total\\n\\n---\\n\\n## etcd Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\n### Architecture\\netcd uses **Raft consensus protocol** for leader election. All nodes participate in a distributed consensus algorithm where only one node can be elected as leader for each term.\\n\\n### Key Components\\n\\n**1. RaftNode (server/etcdserver/raft.go)**\\n- Wraps go.etcd.io/raft/v3 library\\n- Executes ticker loop that periodically calls raft.Tick() for election timeout\\n- Transitions happen via Raft state machine: Follower → Candidate → Leader\\n- Manages heartbeat intervals and election timeouts\\n\\n**2. EtcdServer (server/etcdserver/server.go)**\\n- Top-level server implementing leader detection and failover\\n- Methods: Lead() returns current leader ID, isLeader() checks if local is leader\\n- Tracks leadership changes via raftStatus.Lead field (updated from Raft Ready messages)\\n\\n**3. Leadership Tracking (server/etcdserver/raft.go:start())**\\n- Monitors SoftState.Lead from Raft Ready channel\\n- Detects leader changes and fires updateLeadership callback\\n- Sets metrics: hasLeader (1/0), isLeader (1/0), leaderChanges counter\\n\\n### Leadership Election Mechanism\\n\\n**Election Trigger (server/config/config.go)**\\n- Followers track ElectionTicks (default 10 ticks)\\n- Each tick = TickMs (default 100ms), so election timeout ≈ 1 second\\n- InitialElectionTickAdvance: Fast-forwards ticks on startup to speed initial election\\n- PreVote: Additional phase to minimize disruptive re-elections\\n\\n**State Transitions (Raft-driven)**\\n- **Follower**: Receives heartbeats (AppendEntries) from leader\\n- **Candidate**: On election timeout, campaigns for votes\\n- **Leader**: Wins majority votes, becomes leader and sends heartbeats to all followers\\n\\n**Failover Detection (server/etcdserver/raft.go:start())**\\n- Followers timeout if no heartbeat within ElectionTicks duration\\n- New candidate wins election among remaining nodes\\n- Followers detect new leader from updated SoftState.Lead\\n- Raft guarantees only one leader per term through strict voting rules\\n\\n### Leadership Transfer\\n\\n**Explicit Transfer (server/etcdserver/server.go:MoveLeader())**\\n- Current leader manually transfers leadership to target member\\n- Validates target is not a learner (learners cannot be leaders)\\n- Uses raft.TransferLeadership() to initiate transfer\\n- Waits for Lead() to change to target before returning\\n\\n**Graceful Shutdown (server/etcdserver/server.go:TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown())**\\n- On shutdown, current leader transfers to longest-connected follower\\n- Prevents abrupt leader loss in multi-node clusters\\n- Single-node clusters skip transfer (no targets available)\\n- Timeout: ReqTimeout from configuration\\n\\n### Health and Monitoring\\n- LeaderStats tracks communication with each follower\\n- Heartbeat send failures indicate overloaded disk or network issues\\n- Interceptor (server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/interceptor.go) checks s.Leader() != raft.None\\n- Metrics track leader_changes_seen_total per day\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Lease-based (API objects) | Raft-based (consensus) |\\n| **Timing** | LeaseDuration (15s default) | ElectionTicks (1s default) |\\n| **Failover Detection** | Lease expiration check | Heartbeat timeout in Raft |\\n| **Coordination** | Kubernetes API server | Direct peer-to-peer Raft messages |\\n| **Re-election** | Any expired lease can be acquired | Raft voting ensures safety |\\n| **Transfer** | Manual or timeout-based | MoveLeader() API or graceful shutdown |\\n| **Fault Tolerance** | Depends on API server availability | Byzantine-resilient consensus |\\n| **Scale** | Works for many small clusters | Optimized for single etcd cluster |\\n\\n## Integration Points\\n\\nKubernetes uses etcd to store the Lease objects themselves. When a Kubernetes controller runs leader election, it:\\n1. Creates/updates a Lease object in etcd using Kubernetes API\\n2. etcd replicates this Lease across the cluster using Raft\\n3. The controller observes the Lease field to determine if it holds leadership\\n\\nThis creates a layered architecture where etcd's Raft provides durability, while Kubernetes' lease-based election provides application-level coordination.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":8345,"cache_read_input_tokens":97899,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":8345},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0d4284a1-9fae-47f2-ae4c-c3bbb90ab174","uuid":"d75452b8-7600-4014-a32f-348bb3e9d5d4"}
